Free Talk

Just a Laugh 108

— Hai Ke

▲A—Father. Didn't you say the other day that humans are made of dust?

Father—Yes. Humans, whether male or female, are just crystals of dust.

Son—Then why don't we turn into mud when we drink water?

▲A—The young couple who just moved in next door, I find their faces very familiar. I wonder what their names are.

B—They are newlyweds, still in their honeymoon. They just call each other (Darling) and (Dear), so it's impossible to know their names.

▲A—Do you see that woman sitting in the booth over there? How beautiful she is. I once saved her life.

B—Then you are her great benefactor. But what happened?

A—Last year, when I proposed to her, she said to me, "I'd rather die than marry you." I was compassionate and didn't marry her, thus saving her life.

▲Judge—Your crimes are heinous. I have sentenced you to ten years in prison. Do you have anything to say? Speak quickly.

Criminal—Then for the next ten years, we will have many opportunities to get close. If your husband has free time, please have him visit me often. You'd be most welcome.

A Record of Mr. Li Jianqiu of Jiangyin's Failure in Running Schools 109

— Xue

Mr. Li Jianqiu (Fu) of Jiangyin was once a scholar during the late Qing Dynasty. He was poor but excelled at painting geese and was proficient in calligraphy and all the arts. Therefore, those seeking his work were numerous. Mr. Li used the income from his writing and painting, in addition to supporting his family, entirely for running schools and purchasing calligraphy, paintings, and antiques. Therefore, his family had no permanent assets. Mr. Li founded two schools, one being Huacheng Middle School and the other being Commercial Middle School. The annual expenses of both schools all came from Mr. Li's own efforts. Mr. Li was truly a dedicated educator.

During the Second Revolution of 1913, the southeast was in turmoil. Mr. Li's writings were not without influence. As a result, by the end of that year, he owed Huacheng teachers and staff over two thousand taels of silver in unpaid salaries. As the lunar year drew to a close, there was no way to raise the funds. The teachers and staff all went to Mr. Li's home to demand payment. Mr. Li was extremely anxious. He had no choice but to take six paintings of eagles by Emperor Taizong of the Tang Dynasty from his family's collection and go to Sheng Xingsun in Wujin to sell them. Upon arriving, he had to go through various people to present the paintings to Mr. Sheng. Mr. Sheng looked at the paintings but did not indicate whether he wanted to buy them or not. Instead, he summoned Mr. Li and asked about the paintings' origins. Mr. Li said that the history before the Ming Dynasty was unknown. During the Ming Dynasty, they belonged to Yan Song. During the Qing Dynasty, they were kept in the imperial palace. During the Boxer Rebellion, the treasures of the imperial court were scattered and lost. These paintings also circulated outside. He obtained them in the late Guangxu period from an antique shop in Jinling. Mr. Sheng nodded frequently upon hearing this and said, "These are rare treasures. Since you have them, why are you willing to part with them now?" Mr. Li explained his reasons in detail. Mr. Sheng said, "Your dedication is admirable. But how much do you still owe the teachers and staff in salaries?" Mr. Li replied, "Over two thousand taels of silver." Mr. Sheng immediately took out three thousand taels of silver and gave them to Mr. Li, keeping the paintings. Mr. Li received the money, thanked him, and returned home.

However, Mr. Li misunderstood this as a mortgage, believing that if he had the original amount, he could redeem the paintings sooner or later. This was because Mr. Li believed that neither party had mentioned the value of the paintings. The two thousand taels of silver was only the amount he urgently needed, not the asking price. Mr. Sheng's generous gift of three thousand taels of silver was a temporary act of assistance, not an increased price. Therefore, the following autumn, Mr. Li raised over three thousand taels of silver and went to redeem the paintings. However, Mr. Sheng was surprised and said, "This is a sale, how can it be redeemed? Moreover, the item has already been given away, so it is impossible to comply." Mr. Li was shocked upon hearing this and repeatedly asked people to intercede, but to no avail. Mr. Sheng only agreed to return one thousand taels. Mr. Li knew that he could not salvage the situation, so he took the money and returned home in tears. Upon returning, he told people, "If I had known this would happen, I would have asked for a reasonable price in the first place. But the value is more than just these meager three thousand taels." He was filled with remorse. This matter has been weighing on him for over ten years. Every time he talks about it with people, he is often moved to tears.

The above story was told to me by Mr. Lu Sugong of Jiangyin. Lu and Li were well acquainted and shared the same ideals.

New Couplet for the Flame-Mouth Ceremony 110

— Ji Jin

During the Ghost Festival, it is customary to perform the Flame-Mouth Ceremony. Ordinary monks are extremely busy. In reality, they use this to collect money and spread superstition. I remember Mr. Wu Zhihui, a member of the Central Supervisory Committee, had a couplet that said, "Soliciting alms for ghosts, either worshiping Li or praying to Zhang, collecting sesame seeds to fill a bushel, doing good deeds according to one's ability, not competing for more, not disliking less, just lighting candles and chanting scriptures." He also said, "Humming a few sentences for the public to hear, if not for an outstanding monk, how could he be invited to the seat, scraping together a few coins for immediate use, as long as the money arrives, why not use this opportunity to set up a stage?" The language is humorous and reasonable. I record it here to substantiate this discussion.

Pillowside News by Wang Mei Ju 111

I got up early to draft a piece for the Free Talk section. Just as I was about to send it, my friend Mr. Wu arrived. Upon seeing the title, he laughed and said, "News on the sea, even if it's just a second old, is as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. But how did you get it on your pillow? Did you perhaps dream of Handan and borrow Lu Sheng's magic pillow? Or did you get a jade pillow divinely bestowed like Shen Zong?" I said, "Not so. Last Tuesday, I was slightly ill for three days. Relatives and friends in Shanghai all came to inquire, and each shared the latest news to alleviate my boredom. Today, I got up from my illness and compiled it as follows." After reading it, my friend also said it was worth keeping.

▲It Was I Who Came Not in Spring—On the second day of my illness, my friend Cai Bomin came in the late afternoon. He didn't know I was ill. He said with surprise, "Fortunately, I didn't go with you to the Three Stars Temple magic show the other day." I said that even if I had gone, it wouldn't have caused me to get sick. He said, "No, it's not like that. That day, you didn't go. I was fascinated by Zhang Huichong's water escape trick and knew that the Three Stars performance was only for one day, so I eagerly went. The audience was also eagerly looking forward to it. But just as it was about to begin, a sign suddenly appeared on the stage saying that the glass of the water tank was broken and could not be performed. The crowd was in an uproar. Then the broken glass was placed on the stage, and the curtain was closed. The crowd became even more agitated, clamoring for refunds, but to no avail. They dispersed in disappointment." I laughed and said, "If I had gone with you, then the line 'It was I who came not in spring' wouldn't have been yours alone to lament."

▲Where Did the Heavenly Maiden Come From?—My nephew-in-law Tang Songyuan also came to inquire. I said, "My illness should be getting better soon, but I'm bored because there's no news." Songyuan said, "If you hadn't mentioned it, I would have forgotten. Recently, someone from my hometown (Songyuan is from Hangzhou) said that there is a girl in a family in Xiashicheng, who is eight years old. She is naturally clever and beautiful, but she has an unusual appearance. Her parents keep her hidden and don't let her see anyone. Occasionally, close relatives see her and notice that she has plasters on her cheeks, like big coins. People in Hangzhou are superstitious. Her mother recently believed what a shaman said, that she was born with it and should not hide her true appearance. So she no longer hid her deeply, and the plasters were removed. There are patterns on her cheeks like flowers, complete with branches and leaves, and even pots. The patterns are deep and have artistic meaning. The mother even told people that it's all over her body." I laughed and said, "I suspect it's nonsense if I haven't seen it with my own eyes." Songyuan strongly asserted that it was true. In that case, where did this scattering heavenly maiden come from?

A Small Record of Lanterns at the National Products Emporium 112

— Yang Tian

Since the opening of the Nanjing Road China National Products United Emporium, almost two months have passed. The interior layout is well-organized. The goods on display are mostly of good quality and reasonably priced. All sectors are happy to purchase them, so business is thriving. This is also good news in the movement to promote national products. Considering that visitors had no entertainment, the emporium began on the twelfth of last month to hang riddles in the public lounge on the second floor every night, offering national products as prizes to those who guessed correctly. Mr. Liu Wan'an, Cao Chigong, Wu Lianzhou, and Xue Hanmei were invited to manage the events. Later, due to various commitments, they could not be present every night, so it was changed to hanging lanterns three times a week, on Wednesdays, Saturdays, and Sundays. When the lanterns are lit, colorful banners are displayed. The clever riddle-solvers are happy to come and return full of prizes. I was asked by the gentlemen in charge to write some riddles. I am ashamed of my meager knowledge and could not come up with anything original. Here are some that are close to natural and idiomatic, offered for your criticism. I know I cannot avoid it. "Left home young, returned old." (Answer: A Tang poem—"He xiang sheng bai fa.") "You know, I know." (Answer: A colloquialism—"Tian xiao de.") "Now again." (Answer: A rhyme—"Er. Zhong.") "To praise it." (Answer: A person from the Republic of China—"Chen Qimei.") "Three hangings." (Answer: A story from Liao Zhai—"Yi Xi.") "Farewell." (Answer: A Tang poem—"Zui hou ge fensan.") "Grandparents, parents, children all extravagant." (Answer: A plant—"Dai dai hua.") "Luxuriant pines and cypresses, flower calyxes shining." (Answer: A shop name—"Yi Le Ye.") "A literary tiger's gift." (Answer: Two sentences from The Doctrine of the Mean—"Si ze de zhi. Bu si ze bu de ye.") "Only the wandering official." (Answer: A story from Liao Zhai—"Yi Yuan Guan.") "Leaguer late in life with many bumps and bruises." (Answer: A Tang poem—"Xiang wan yi bu shi.") "I am a husband." (Answer: A character—"Yu.") "Originally a department store, suddenly the home of an emperor." (Answer: A Peking opera—"Yong An Gong.") "Spring flower." (Answer: A story from Liao Zhai—"Wu Qiuyue.") "Pediatrician." (Answer: Two stories from Liao Zhai—"Bao Wang. Ying Ning.") "Only eats lunch." (Answer: Two sentences from The Doctrine of the Mean—"Chao bu shi. Xi bu shi.") "Woman." (Answer: An ancient beauty's name—"Juan Lian. Nv Ying.") "Double stars should regret." (Answer: Six Talents—"Hui shao li duo.") "Although Russia is now ruled by the Red Party, it will inevitably fail in the future." (Answer: Two names from Water Margin—"Shi Qian. Bai Sheng.") "Who caused the May Thirtieth Incident?" (Answer: A character—"Hui.") "Two Shu entangled, difficult to fulfill the wish of aviation." (Answer: A Tang poem—"Shen su fei bing zai chuang.") "Not from a legitimate origin." (Answer: A story from Liao Zhai—"Ji Sheng.") "The theory opposes Su Ji, and the beauty bestows the title of Mang Daifu." (Answer: Two names from Water Margin—"Zhang Heng. Wu Song.") "The mummy has gone." (Answer: A story from Liao Zhai—"Shi Bian.") "Eyes like torches." (Answer: Two names from Water Margin—"Kong Ming. Kong Liang.")

Dissent of the Roman Curia Regarding Chinese Customs (Continued) 113

— Li Liu Zeng, Sent from Paris

At this time, the Jesuit order in Paris gradually lost ground. In 1708, a man named Malebranche published a work fiercely criticizing Chinese customs, which attracted much attention at the time. The Roman side was also completely controlled by the Dominican order. At the beginning of 1708, a Jesuit priest named Provana returned from China, carrying a letter from Emperor Kangxi and records of previous declarations and arbitrations issued to teachers of both orders. He requested an audience with the Pope. Pope Clement XI not only refused to meet him but also immediately officially published the Church's accusations against Chinese customs, which had been secretly delivered to the special envoy to China, Tournon, in 1704.

At that time, public opinion was extremely interested in the Chinese customs issue, which had caused endless disputes. Discussions took place everywhere, and there was no consensus. In order to end the dispute, the Pope, on September 25, 1710, ordered by the Tribunal of the Holy Office that anyone who discussed this issue without special permission would be excommunicated. This order is the most recent order by the Tribunal of the Holy Office to reaffirm its validity. The matter has passed two centuries since then. According to the July 25 POsservatore romano, many people recently doubted whether this 1710 order was still valid. Therefore, the cardinals of the Holy See gathered on the 18th to reaffirm its value.

Looking at the course of this matter, the Holy See lightly believed one side's words and arbitrarily slandered traditional Chinese customs with a dogmatic attitude, which is truly regrettable. We should know that the struggle between the Dominican order and the Jesuit order, although nominally a religious issue, was actually a struggle between France and Spain for political power in China. The successful position of the Jesuit order in China was the basis for French colonization in China. Not only did the Spanish not want this, but the Roman Curia was also deeply uneasy about the possibility that all religious authority in China would be controlled by the French. The Jesuit order, supported by the French government, disregarded the Pope's orders. From this, we can see the divisions within the Catholic Church. The so-called Pope is merely a figurehead.

For two hundred years, Catholic power in China was entirely protected by France, with little direct relationship with the Holy See. Recently, since the Italian government and the Vatican signed a treaty, the Pope, with a more stable foundation for the Holy See, has gradually intended to reclaim Catholic power in China from the hands of the French. Why was this ban on Chinese customs, issued in 1710, suddenly brought up? Why did the Holy See reaffirm it? There must be some political background in it, which cannot be viewed simply as a simple religious issue.

Heartwarming Thoughts (271) 114

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 14: Green Bamboo Tears Stain Her Face, Brokenhearted; Red Lotus Fragrance Fades, a Maiden's Soul Leaves

Cuiyun thought, for the sake of the old master, she shouldn't argue anymore, right? What happened before was certainly hateful. But now, she is childless, having not given birth to a son or daughter, which is also very pitiful. Who knew that as Cuiyun began to feel a little free and comfortable, she suffered another major illness. People in their circle of the Qu Garden were most afraid of getting sick. Originally, sending invitations to summon flowers and calling for singers was very lively. After a few calls, when it was said that she was still not well, the guests became scarce. Or they would go and find another establishment. If they had their own small house, they could recover from their illness there. But Cuiyun didn't have her own house, so she spent her days groaning in a small attic. At first, a few guests came to check on her, but when they entered her room, a smell of medicine mixed with the smell of illness made people uncomfortable. In Chinese sickrooms, the windows are always closed tightly, so the air inside is even worse. Adding to that the patient's pale and emaciated face, frowning and bitter expression, which made people uncomfortable, people regarded her room as a dangerous place. So, in the latter half of her illness, let alone anyone making advances, not even a ghost would visit her door. She suffered from typhoid fever for a full month. But the business for the next quarter had to be struggled for. If she were to rest for a quarter, where would the expenses come from? Fortunately, her illness gradually improved, but after the illness, her appearance was haggard. Even her hair fell out like autumn leaves, revealing sparse patches on her head. Who would spend money to see your sick face? After enduring for a month or two, her body gradually recovered, and she became even more energetic and full of spirit than before her illness. Business slowly recovered. When Zuo Shichen met her, it was two or three months after she had recovered from her illness. Later, Cuiyun married someone, and after that, Zuo Shichen no longer contacted her. It turned out that the man Cuiyun married was also a businessman from Shanghai. His ancestral home was Ningbo, but he had been in Shanghai for many years. Since Shanghai opened up as a trading port, people from two places have been the most successful. They each have their own strong vigor in the business world. One place is Guangdong, and the other is Ningbo. Although the people of Guangdong have strong assets and are skilled at maneuvering, their pioneering and rugged efforts are far inferior to those of the Ningbo people. Moreover, they are willing to endure hardship. Often, those who arrive in Shanghai wearing a simple blue cloth gown become famous in the business world in less than ten years. This is because they have the courage to be enterprising. At first, they willingly endure humiliation, but once they gain power, they extend their power. Therefore, many come from humble backgrounds, such as being a Western servant, a groom, or a lighterman. But once they have an opportunity, they can seize it and use it for their own benefit. Originally, "heroes are not afraid of low origins." Even emperors have risen from humble origins. How much more so for businessmen?

Yarn, Cotton, and Cotton Yarn Markets Trend Upward 120

The yarn market turned upward, mainly because American cotton rebounded, leading to slightly stronger confidence. The market atmosphere stabilized, and Ruidi, a major short seller, purchased a large amount to cover their positions, driving up the market. However, spot yarn sales have become increasingly quiet, with no transactions from various groups. According to some sources, most of the goods shipped by the Guangdong group the day before were stored locally and not moving. Local inventory prices are gradually increasing, reportedly around 130,000 to 140,000 bales. Therefore, the Guangdong group, seeing the unfavorable situation, closed out their forward yarn positions in Shanghai, selling a lot recently. The future of the yarn market still depends on actual demand.

▲Large Human Label Operators Cover Shorts: The human label market opened with a stronger atmosphere due to rising American cotton and fewer sellers. Large operators covered their short positions, tightening the market further. Prices for all months rose by 0.06, 0.07, 0.08, and 0.09 yuan. In the afternoon, due to positive news about American cotton, buying interest was stronger, but actual sales were sluggish, and prices for all months rose again by 0.02 or 0.05 yuan. The Cotton Market Shows a Beautiful Upward Trend 121

▲Good News for American Cotton · Unpredictable Weather:

The cotton market is firm again, mainly due to the rise in American cotton and the unpredictable weather, which has tightened confidence. Buying interest has increased sharply, coupled with Ruidi covering shorts. However, some Han groups sold slightly due to high prices, while factories still had no intention to transact, and actual sales remained sluggish.

American Cotton Recovered Strongly Last Week 125

▲Southern United States Still Has Cotton Hoarding Movement

▲Manufacturers Pay Attention to Contracts for 1923

A telegram dated the 5th reports on the cotton market situation for the week: The increase in short selling in the South at the beginning of the week and the loosening of actual positions caused cotton prices to fall. However, when the price of new cotton for October delivery fell to around 11 cents, short covering stopped the decline. Subsequently, due to the lack of weakness in futures and continued hoarding in the South, prices recovered. However, before the release of the Department of Agriculture's report, many began to sell, resulting in price fluctuations. Private estimates of cotton production range from 52.4% to 56.0% under normal conditions, with harvests ranging from 13,420,000 bales to 14,664,000 bales. Therefore, people are increasingly uncertain about the government's estimated quantity for next Monday. Many areas in the South are suffering from local drought, and it is also heard that Eastern cotton is underdeveloped and that yields in Louisiana and Texas are poor.

Also, it is reported that the Department of Agriculture's cotton production report is predicted to average around 14 million bales, with some short covering as a result. The South continues to show a hoarding trend. Domestic piece goods trade has slightly better demand. Manufacturers are now paying attention to contracts for 1923 goods.

Local Yarn Inventory Increases Sharply 127

▲Chinese and British Yarn Increases, Japanese Yarn Decreases

According to a survey by Japanese firms, the yarn inventory at the end of August was 132,024 bales, an increase of 13,799 bales compared to the previous month. Chinese and British factory yarn accounted for 123,279 bales, an increase of 16,249 bales compared to the previous month. Japanese factory yarn accounted for 4,745 bales, a decrease of 2,450 bales.

Grains: Foreign Rice and Ke Xian Rice Sales are Both Sluggish 128

▲Foreign Rice: The market was even more sluggish yesterday, with no sales from either the Northern or Southern groups. There were also no inquiries from Zhejiang or the mainland. The small-grained rice returned from Hankou has yet to find a buyer. Fortunately, the inventory is very small, so prices have not fallen sharply. The overall market saw only Min Dang of this street purchase 100 bags, Saigon No. 1 100 bags, and small-grained brown rice 100 bags.

▲Ke Xian Rice: Ke Xian rice from Jiangxi and Hunan continues to arrive. Because Ke Xian rice is not moving, the market remains dull. However, sales from this street have gradually improved after the flat price system was gradually abolished. Purchasing power in the market is also better than last month. Although the arriving Ke Xian rice is not moving, this street and the countryside still have an appetite, so the market has been able to stand firm. It is estimated that over 1,000 bags of early Jiangxi machine rice and 500 bags of late machine rice were sold. Hunan Jinggang rice 390 bags. Sales prices for each commodity are listed in the market price table.

Flour Market Shows a Lively Trend 129

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market for each month showed a firm and lively trend. Because foreign wheat quotations rebounded by 0.05, 0.06, or 0.07 yuan, sentiment has turned from sluggish to stable. The enthusiastic bulls believe that the ban on sales to the North will hopefully be lifted in the next few days. Therefore, the bulls for this month believe that once the North is open for sales, the quiet market can definitely turn active. Therefore, buying interest was very strong for a time, and the prices for each month in the coming period were also raised. Observing this phenomenon, it is possible that factories with goods will have to continue to hold up prices for this month because foreign flour cannot be shipped in any way. In the afternoon, the atmosphere for each month remained stable, but showed a fluctuating trend, with little increase in prices. As a result, prices for this month and October each rose by 0.0175 yuan, November rose by 0.015 yuan, December and January rose by 0.0075 yuan, and February rose by 0.0125 yuan.

Recent Wheat Slightly Recovered 130

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat market in the afternoon, the market for each month had turned stable. Because foreign wheat quotations rebounded and wheat flour was about to be opened for sale to the North, sentiment for both near-term and long-term wheat was raised. Although there is a large stock of current wheat for this month and the factory appetite is not very good, it should be seen as flat and weak in theory. However, because the standards cannot be met, most of the wheat cannot be delivered. Therefore, some of the short positions are still being covered at any time, so the market is still being held up. As a result, this month is up 0.02 yuan compared to the previous day, November is up 0.01 yuan, January is up 0.01 yuan, and the rest are unchanged. Various factories are still holding on to current wheat and have no intention to move. Only Huafeng ate 2,000 bags of Xuzhou Dangshan wheat, with the price nearly 0.01 yuan lower than a few days ago.

Silk and Tea: European and American Silk Sales are in a State of Collapse 132

Yesterday's Shanghai foreign firm silk market continued to be dull. Overseas markets have sent telegrams complaining that Shanghai's yellow and white silk, etc., are too expensive due to the cheap competition from Japanese silk, and there have been no inquiries. Only Hulin entered five packages of Longma brand top-grade Shanghai white factory silk, with 13 to 22 filaments, at a price of only 980 taels. The rest were all silent.

New York Japanese Silk Prices Continue to Fall 133

▲Factories Seek to Reduce Costs · Japanese Merchants Compete at Low Prices

Recently, the New York market has been increasingly lifeless. Since the economic downturn, each silk weaving factory has been striving to reduce costs for its products. Raw silk materials are generally only purchased when cheap, resulting in dull and lifeless silk sales. Japanese silk merchants cater to the psychology of the factories and sell Japanese silk cheaply, making silk prices even lower. At the beginning of the month, A-grade Japanese silk was only priced at US$3.30 per pound, B-grade at US$2.80, and C-grade at US$2.25.

Gaozhuang Zhenmei Tea Transactions are Smooth and Prosperous 134

Yesterday, the interest of Wu Yuan Gaozhuang Zhenmei, Dudu, Tianxiang, and Jinlong firms remained strong. Overall market transactions were not sluggish, and the market showed a slightly firm trend. However, medium and low-grade tea remained stagnant. Gongxi green tea and Russian firm tea have not moved. Baitouzhuang tea also remained mostly in observation. The overall trend remains poor.

Hardware: San Zhang Big Guangzhou Leather Scarce and Prices Rise 135

San Zhang Big Guangzhou Leather has been procured frequently by the military recently, leading to a shortage of spot goods in the market. The market was searched yesterday and was very scarce. Prices soared by 0.03 or 0.04 yuan, with Xinzhong at 9.35 taels. However, there are still many buyers.

Local News

City Party Headquarters Prepares to Commemorate the Premier's First Uprising 152

September 9th is the anniversary of the Premier's first uprising. The Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters has specifically scheduled a commemorative meeting to be held at 9:00 AM on this day at the Xiaoximen Youth Propaganda Group in the South City. Party headquarters, agencies, and groups at all levels in the city must send four representatives to attend at the designated time.

Today

Citywide Special Martial Law 153

▲Strict Defense in Both the Chinese and Foreign Concessions

Today is the 9/7 commemoration, and military and police defenses have been strengthened. A special martial law has been declared throughout the city. Details are as follows:

▲Garrison Command Office Operates Day and Night The Songhu Garrison Command has decided to follow the May 1st method, ordering its affiliated military and police agencies to comply. Although today is a regular Sunday holiday, the department will still operate as usual. The two departments of the staff and adjutant are primarily responsible, and there is no rest day or night.

▲Two Railways Police Extra Patrols Kong Fanjun, the police chief of the Beijing-Shanghai and Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, specifically telegraphed each section police chief of the two railways yesterday, saying: Today's commemoration has arrived again, and it is feared that reactionary elements will take the opportunity to riot. Now that military affairs on the front lines are progressing, it is sincerely feared that the rebel army will collude with reactionaries to disturb the rear. The two railways are important for transportation, and bridges and roads should be strictly guarded. From 6:00 AM on the 7th to 6:00 PM on the 8th, stop resting and return to patrol. All must be armed and diligently patrol, without the slightest slack. Be sure to comply with this order.

▲Defense of the British and French Concessions The military and police agencies in the city have been ordered to take precautions, so since yesterday, the defenses in the north and south of the city have been greatly strengthened. The iron gates along the Chinese border in the Public Concession and the French Concession have only opened one gate in areas with more pedestrian traffic to allow vehicles to pass through. The iron gates in other secluded alleyways are all closed. Fei, the chief inspector of the French Concession Police Department, sent a large number of workers yesterday to carry the barbed wire frames to the Avenue Edward VII along the border between the British and French concessions, such as the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Rue de Montigny, the intersection of West New Bridge Street, the intersection of Rue de l'Arquebuse, the intersection of East New Bridge Street, the intersection of Rue du Père Huc, and the intersection of Rue de la Cathédrale, etc., and placed them on the sidewalks on both sides. The iron gates at the road intersections in the Xujiahui Bridge West Gate and the Avenue de la République along the Chinese-French border have all been selectively closed, and additional Chinese and Vietnamese police have been dispatched to patrol back and forth without stopping.

Wang Zhengting Went to Hangzhou Yesterday 154

▲The Takeover of Weihaiwei Will Not Be Delayed

▲The British Envoy May Come to Beijing on the 8th to Negotiate

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting arrived in Shanghai by express train from Beijing at 9:00 PM the night before. At 10:00 AM yesterday, he went to the Foreign Affairs Discussion Association office on Avenue Joffre to meet with Wu Tianfang, assistant to the Intelligence Department, and Xu Zushan, the commissioner of the Foreign Ministry preparing for the takeover of Weihaiwei. According to Wang's statement to this newspaper's reporter, the takeover of Weihaiwei will definitely take place on October 1st. In any case, it will not be delayed. The rumors are completely untrustworthy. British Minister Lampson set off from Beidaihe on the 5th and is coming south. He will arrive in Beijing on the 8th to discuss this matter with me, as well as the issue of recovering the British Concession in Xiamen. As for the takeover method, the Foreign Ministry has prepared everything properly and is just waiting for the National Government to appoint a commissioner. The Sino-Japanese telecommunications negotiations are being handled jointly by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Communications. The Foreign Ministry is currently in contact with the Ministry of Communications, and there is no definite date for the meeting. There have been no new developments in the Sino-Russian negotiations, and so on. Xu Zushan also said that I went to Weihaiwei for more than a month and repeatedly contacted Johnson, the British Weihaiwei Commissioner, to negotiate the takeover procedures and details, and we have already agreed on everything. I have already reported to the Foreign Ministry. As for the Reuters news report that the British Parliament is questioning China's takeover of Weihaiwei, from my personal observation, the U.S. government's right to ratify foreign treaties ultimately rests with Congress. Congress can veto the president's ratification of foreign treaties, but this is not the case in the United Kingdom. Looking at the recent three hundred years of American diplomatic history, although the final ratification right rests with Congress, no matter that has been approved by the British monarch after consulting with the Congressional Foreign Affairs Group has ever been rejected. Therefore, the takeover of Weihaiwei on October 1st will definitely not be extended. The National Government has not yet appointed a takeover commissioner. I am only responsible for diplomatic matters, and so on. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Wang went to Hangzhou with his family for sightseeing and is scheduled to return to Shanghai today. He will go to Beijing that evening to take up his duties. Chinese Taxpayer Association

Important Telegrams Dispatched Yesterday 155

▲ Chinese Directors to Take Over, Report to Government

▲ Special Committee to Deal with Water Prices

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association yesterday, based on the resolution of the delegates' conference the day before, issued seven telegrams, recorded as follows: ▲ Regarding the Replacement of Chinese Directors

▲ Telegram to Government Authorities: To the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ministry of Interior, Ministry of Finance of the National Government of Nanjing, the Jiangsu Provincial Government of Zhenjiang, the Special Commissioner's Office for Finance of Jiangsu, and the Shanghai Municipal Government: Mr. Bei Songsun, the director representing the Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association to the Shanghai Municipal Council, has been assigned by the Bank of China to inspect banking operations in Europe and America for more than six months. He has requested to resign. Our association convened a delegates' conference on September 5th. Due to the circumstances, we could not retain him. It was resolved that Mr. Bei Songsun's resignation be approved, and a replacement should be elected immediately. As a result of the election, Mr. Hu Mengjia was elected to succeed him as the director to the Shanghai Municipal Council. In addition to separate letters, we hereby telegraph this for your review and record. It is for the public good. Wang Xiaolai and Xu Jilong, Chairmen of the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association, kowtow. (The letter to various local organizations is omitted.)

▲ Letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council: Respectfully, Mr. Bei Songsun, the director representing our association to your council, has resigned due to his departure to inspect banking operations overseas. Mr. Hu Mengjia has now been appointed to succeed him. We hereby inform you and request that you take note of this matter. Addressed to the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council.

▲ Regarding the Water Price Increase

▲ Letter to the Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council: The association yesterday sent a letter to Mr. Macnaghten, Chairman of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council, stating: Respectfully, the issue of increasing the price of tap water in the Public Concession was discussed at our association's delegates' conference on September 5th. It was resolved that this matter, which increases the burden on residents, needs to be seriously reconsidered. In addition to instructing the Executive Committee to form a special committee for thorough research, we request that your council suspend the implementation of the proposed price increase to comply with the public opinion of the residents. We specially record this matter and send it to you, hoping for your review and action, and we look forward to your response.

▲ Letter to the Five Chinese Directors: Another letter was sent to the Chinese directors Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Liu Hongsheng, and Hu Mengjia, stating: Respectfully, the issue of increasing the price of tap water in the Public Concession was discussed at our association's delegates' conference on September 5th. It was resolved that (1) this matter, which increases the burden on residents, needs to be seriously reconsidered, and a letter should be sent to the Municipal Council to suspend the implementation of the proposed price increase; (2) the Shanghai Real Estate Association should be informed that new water contracts should still be calculated at the old price; (3) detailed countermeasures should be submitted to the Executive Committee to form a special committee for review and action. In addition to separate notifications, we hereby record this matter and send it to you, hoping for your review and action.

▲ Reply to the Shanghai Real Estate Association: Respectfully replying, we received your letter stating that the 25% increase in the price of tap water in the Public Concession, implemented since September 1st, has a significant and profound impact on the lives of millions of residents in the concession. You have listed the reasons and opinions against it, and requested our assistance. Upon review, this matter was proposed for opposition by Committee Member Chu Fucheng at the Executive Committee meeting of our association on August 29th. After discussion, it was decided that due to the importance of the matter, it should be submitted to the delegates' conference for a decision. Upon receiving your letter, it was submitted to the delegates' conference on the 5th of this month. It was agreed that the increase in tap water prices would increase the burden on residents and that it was necessary to seriously reconsider the matter. A letter should be sent to the Municipal Council to suspend the implementation of the price increase. At the same time, the Shanghai Real Estate Association should be informed that all new water contracts should still be calculated based on the 6% water price. The detailed countermeasures were to be submitted to the Executive Committee to form a special committee for review and action. In addition to informing the Municipal Council and convening the Executive Committee, we hereby record this matter and reply, hoping that your association will notify all members that all new water contracts should still be calculated at the old price. This is our sincere hope.

▲ Regarding Chinese Directors and Tap Water

▲ Letter to All Executive Committee Members: Respectfully, it is hereby decided to convene the Executive Committee at 4:00 PM on the 8th of this month at the association's building at No. 4 Hong Kong Road to discuss the following two important matters: (A) Mr. Hu Mengjia, a standing committee member of our association, has been elected by the delegates' conference to replace the Chinese director to the Shanghai Municipal Council, leaving a vacancy in the standing committee, which should be filled immediately; (B) The proposed increase in the price of tap water in the Public Concession has been resolved by the delegates' conference to be submitted to the Executive Committee to form a special committee for detailed review and countermeasures. The above two matters, one concerning the internal organization of our association and the other concerning the increased burden on residents, are both of extreme importance. We earnestly hope that you will attend the meeting on time to facilitate progress. We await your presence.

Special District to Start Selling Rice 156

▲ Sales Start on the 9th at the Tianhou Temple

The Shanghai Rice Market Regulation Committee is procuring rice to be sold in the special district of the concessions. It is reported that Mr. Lu Wenshao, a leader in the rice industry, has made arrangements. The sales location is the old site of the Tianhou Temple on North Henan Road. The municipal party headquarters has instructed the three district party headquarters to borrow the location. At the same time, the municipal rice merchant association has appointed Wang Weiquan, Lu Shaolian, Lu Guishan, Ge Peiyuan, and Luo Zipei to be responsible for the affairs there. The price of the rice is currently set at 380 copper coins per liter, equivalent to about 13 yuan per stone, which is about 3 yuan cheaper than the market price. Each person can buy a maximum of five dou and a minimum of two sheng. The sales hours are from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM. It has been confirmed that sales will begin on the 9th of this month. The municipal chamber of commerce has also sent letters to the municipal police bureau and the Shanghai Public Concession Police Department, requesting that police officers be dispatched to the site to maintain order.

Local News

Discovery of Genuine Cholera 157

▲ Citizens Must Be Cautious About Hygiene

This summer, the incidence of epidemics in Shanghai was rare, and the number of outpatients at various epidemic hospitals was significantly lower than in previous years. Genuine cholera was also not found. Unexpectedly, since the beginning of autumn, the dreaded cholera has been found. Yesterday, the Shanghai Red Cross Society's epidemic hospital found a patient named Jin Fuquan. The results of the examination by the Shanghai Municipal Council's health department confirmed that he had genuine cholera. The examination report has been sent to the hospital. It is reported that the hospital admitted two more patients yesterday, also similar to cholera, but the examination reports from the health department have not yet been received. It is also reported that several cases have been found in the Hongkou Epidemic Hospital.

Record of the Municipal District Planning Committee 158

The Municipal Organization Law has been promulgated for some time, and the division of districts is indeed an important matter within the city. The law stipulates that it must be completed within three months after the promulgation of the law. The municipal government believes that Shanghai should also prepare for this, so it appointed Councilor Xu Peihuang and others as committee members. The first meeting was held at the municipal government at 9:00 AM yesterday. All committee members and representatives attended the meeting. Xu Peihuang was elected as chairman and declared the meeting open. The matters decided after separate discussions are mainly: (1) The district division work must be completed within two months from today; (2) The city has a dense population, and the original system of five households per neighborhood is not applicable. It is necessary to request the Ministry of Interior to make changes based on the special circumstances; (3) The number of households must be verified if there are discrepancies, and July should be used as the standard month; (4) Boat dwellers, except for those with land-based residences, should be distributed based on the survey results; (5) Two groups will be formed: a general affairs group and a survey group. The members of the various bureaus of the municipal government belong to the general affairs group, and the members of the various municipal affairs committees or their representatives and the members of the public security bureau belong to the survey group. The discussion that day strictly followed the law and facts, and everyone tried their best to clarify the true meaning until after 12:00 PM before the meeting adjourned.

Reorganization Plan for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company 159

▲ Li Zhonggong to Return to Shanghai Soon

Li Zhonggong plans to go to Shanghai on the 9th or 10th, but the date of his assumption of office has not yet been decided. Of the nine members of the reorganization committee, the government will first appoint four or five, and the rest will be filled by those from Shanghai's industrial, shipping, and banking sectors who are willing to cooperate. The reorganization plan, whether it is government-run, commercially-run, a joint government-commercial venture, or government-supervised commercial operation, must choose the most appropriate option. The prerequisite is that one party must value national operations, and the other party must consider the rights of commercial shareholders. As for the back wages of employees and overdue interest coupons, which are related to the livelihood of employees and external credit, huge sums of money must first be raised to pay them separately. In the future, more than one million yuan must be raised each month to cope with the situation.

Hearing on the Jin Li Yuan Case Yesterday 160

▲ French Side Has No Reply Regarding Lease Renewal and Purchase

▲ China Merchants Bureau Sent Letter to French Consul-General Yesterday to Make a Statement

▲ The San De Tang Should Be Responsible for the Delay in Negotiations

The China Merchants Bureau is in dispute with the French side over the Jin Li Yuan Wharf case. The negotiations have not progressed smoothly, and the deadline for the French Court to execute the termination of the contract is approaching. The San De Tang should be responsible for the delay. Yesterday, a letter was sent to French Consul-General Ganglering, stating: Respectfully, our bureau's arbitrator, lawyer Gao Shuo, recently stated that on the 1st of this month (i.e., Monday), he and Mr. Lu Bohong visited Father Xia Lou and verbally agreed to send a telegram to the Paris headquarters to request instructions on the selling price. After inquiring by telegram in recent days, it was said that no reply had been received. Our bureau is extremely willing to resolve this matter as soon as possible to promote friendship. Moreover, the deadline of September 15th agreed upon by the former Consul-General is approaching. If the priest has to telegraph Paris for instructions on everything, it may not be possible to resolve the matter within the time limit. The San De Tang should be held responsible for the delay. Please inform the French Court accordingly. This is a special statement. Wishing you good health, this is addressed to French Consul-General Gan. Cai Pei, General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau.

Vigilance in Yangtze River Shipping 161

▲ Shengjing Vessel Fights Bandits in Qizhou: The Taikoo Company's Yangtze River vessel Shengjing, returning to Shanghai from Hankou this time, was attacked by bandits when it was near Wuxue, downstream of Qizhou. It was late at night, and there were many passengers on board, all sound asleep. Suddenly, rifle fire erupted from both banks like a string of pearls, and many passengers were awakened from their dreams. Fortunately, the ship had hired six British sailors and two machine guns in Hankou. The British soldiers opened fire on the bandits on both banks with machine guns for about twenty minutes before the bandits retreated. Although the Shengjing vessel was attacked by bandits, fortunately, no one was injured.

▲ Taishun Vessel Encounters Warning Sound: The China Merchants Bureau's Taishun vessel, traveling upstream from Nanjing to Hankou, was suddenly fired upon by lurking bandits on the banks of the Yangtze River at a place called Zeyin. It was night, so the Taishun vessel turned off its lights and sailed quickly to avoid being targeted by the bandits. Although the hull was hit by several bullets, no one was injured. Foreign warships are now protecting ships from Daye to Hankou, while Chinese ships are installing bulletproof plates to ensure safety.

▲ Hongheng Docks at Shashi: The Sanbei Company received a telegram from Shashi stating that bandits are rampant in the four rural villages there. After the Hongheng vessel arrived in Shashi, it originally planned to return to Hankou immediately, but it has been retained by the merchants and residents of Shashi, who have requested that it remain docked for one more day, so that they can take the ship to Hankou for temporary refuge in case of emergency, to avoid being extorted for huge sums of money by foreign ships. In addition, the company's Wuxing vessel was detained between Wanxian and Yichang for smuggling contraband. It has not been released because the fine of 20,000 yuan has not been paid in full. The Sanbei Company has telegraphed Liu Xiang to order its release.

Red Cross Society's Committee to Revise Articles of Association 162

▲ Fifth Meeting

The China Red Cross Society's Committee to Revise Articles of Association held its fifth meeting at 2:00 PM on the 5th of this month. The members present were Li Zhenbang, Hong Yanbin, Jiang Daqiu, Yang Ke, Wang Peiyuan, Xue Shaoting, Liu Hongsheng, Wen Lanting, Wu Jiasan, Ye Zhisheng, Wang Xiaolai, and other committee members. Chairman Wen Lanting presided over the meeting. After the usual formalities, the minutes of the previous meeting were read, and there were no objections. The chairman signed them. The chairman stated that the articles of association of the Red Cross Society should be presented for the third reading today. Wu Jiasan stated that the name of the association should be changed to the Red Cross Society of the Republic of China. A vote was taken, and the majority approved. The name of the articles of association was changed to the Red Cross Society of the Republic of China, abbreviated as the Chinese Red Cross Society. Article 1 of the articles of association was changed to "This association is an international charitable organization, organized by members of this association, named the Red Cross Society of the Republic of China, abbreviated as the Chinese Red Cross Society." Hong Yanbin stated that Article 6, Item 2, "A nursing school is attached to the general hospital," is inconsistent with Article 5, Item 3, "Training volunteer doctors and nurses." It should be changed to "A volunteer doctor and nurse school is attached to the general hospital." Jiang Daqiu stated that Article 14 should be changed to "The election method of its representatives and the number of representatives to be sent shall be determined separately." Hong Yanbin stated that Article 18 should be changed to "The Executive Committee shall be composed of eleven executive members elected by the standing executive members." In addition, Article 23, Item 3, should be changed to "Specially awarding honorary members, special members, and awarding various medals." Also, the order of the items in Article 24 should be changed to (1) Handling matters with the government and various agencies, (2) Reviewing the qualifications of joining members, (3) Approving the establishment of branches, (4) Supervising the affairs of the branches, (5) Supervising subordinate institutions, (6) Compiling budgets and final accounts. Jiang Daqiu stated that Yang Yao seconded that whether the standing members and executive members are voluntary positions should be clearly stipulated. The majority approved, and Article 28 was changed to "The term of office of the standing council members and executive members is three years, and they can be re-elected, but they are all voluntary positions." Also, Article 30 is not complete and should be changed to "A request from one-fifth or more of the total number of branches or one-tenth or more of the total number of members shall convene an extraordinary meeting." Wu Jiasan stated that the sentence "All are elected by the executive committee members" should be added under Article 19. In Article 30, the sentence "Convened by the Standing Council within six weeks" is too short and should be changed to "two months." Yang Ke stated that the word "purpose" in Article 31 should be changed to "matter." Hong Yanbin stated that the word "money" in Article 38, Item 2, should be changed to "silver." The section on branches reporting all their property to the general association, which then forwards it for record, should be changed to a separate article after Article 53. Jiang Daqiu stated that the word "house" in Article 38, Item 3, should be changed to "property." Hong Yanbin stated that in Articles 45, 46, and 62, "aircraft" should be added to each item where transportation of materials, etc., may require the use of aircraft. In the sentence "The agency that may temporarily submit a request shall handle it in accordance with the military law of the army and navy personnel," the word "air" should be added. Jiang Daqiu stated that Article 47 should be changed to "In the event of war, the term of office of all standing members and executive members may be extended, but not for more than one year." Wu Jiasan stated that branches should receive subsidies from the general association, and this should be retained in the old regulations. The majority approved and changed the old regulations to "They may receive subsidies from the general association and local government offices." Also, Article 54 still needs to be studied. Xue Shaoting seconded, and it was resolved to change it to "Re-appoint representatives to attend the standing council meeting and express their opinions as executive members." Hong Yanbin stated that the sentence "The general rules for branches shall be determined separately" in Article 55 can be deleted and should be changed to after Article 49. Jiang Daqiu stated that the order of Item 4 in Article 56 must be changed to "4. For those who have contributed to the association, medals may be awarded based on their achievements. The above medals must be decided by the standing council." Xue Shaoting stated that the sentence at the end of Article 57, Item 4, should be added with the words "donation," changed to "However, the membership fees and donations paid will not be refunded." Wu Jiasan, Ye Zhisheng, Jiang Daqiu, Hong Yanbin, and Yang Ke spoke successively, stating that Articles 58 and 59 of the supplementary rules should be discussed in detail and properly revised. It was resolved to delete the words "Articles 58 and 59" and change them to "Items 1 and 2." Jiang Daqiu changed them to "(1) These articles of association shall take effect after being approved by the membership meeting and submitted to the government for record; (2) Amendments to these articles of association must be passed by more than half of the representatives attending the national membership meeting." The chairman proposed that the articles of association of the association have been completed with the third reading and that the branch rules and the election method for standing members should be revised immediately. Meetings will continue every day from next Tuesday (September 9th) at 2:00 PM. The meeting adjourned after the discussion, which was already past 5:00 PM.

Various Places in Shanghai Purchasing Firearms

Should First Submit to the Ministry of Military Administration for Review 163

▲ The Municipal Government Yesterday Ordered the Public Security Bureau and Security Corps to Comply

The municipal government yesterday instructed the Public Security Bureau and the Security Corps Reorganization Committee, stating: For compliance with the order, it is hereby ordered that, upon investigation, various provinces, cities, and counties purchasing firearms in Shanghai should first hand over the funds to the Ministry of Finance's Shanghai office for them to order on their behalf, in order to simplify procedures and save costs. This has been divided into orders for the Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Military Administration, and the various provincial and municipal governments to comply with. In addition, Directive No. 156 from the National Government has been submitted and approved for record. According to the Ministry of Military Administration's reply, after receiving the order, it should be complied with. However, the Ministry has carefully studied the use of firearms purchased by various provinces and counties, whether the purchase should be approved, and the number of firearms to be approved. It seems that the court should clearly order the various provincial and municipal counties to first consult the Ministry for review, and after the review is completed, the Ministry should submit it to the National Government for approval and issuance of passports. At the same time, consult the Ministry of Finance for review. In this way, the ordering will be more unified and checked, and the ordering will be reviewed before and after. Before receiving the order, in addition to complying with the order, all provinces and cities are requested to clearly order, and in the future, when purchasing firearms, they should first submit the use and number to the Ministry for review before applying for a permit and sending it to the Ministry of Finance's Shanghai office for ordering matters. Whether all the reasons are appropriate should be submitted for review in writing, and it is hoped that instructions will be given for compliance, which is for the public good. Therefore, in addition to ordering approval to be handled as instructed, and ordering the Ministry of Finance and the various provincial and municipal governments to comply with the order, it is also ordered that the municipal government should immediately comply with the order.

National Exports to the United States

Decreased by 24 Percent Compared to the Same Period Last Year 165

The Great American Evening News reported that, according to statistics from the US Consulate General, the total exports from China to the United States in the seven months from January to July of this year decreased by 24 percent compared to the same period last year. This year, the total value was US$74,518,312, while last year it was US$103,518,312, a difference of US$28,617,870. The difference in July alone was even more significant. This year, it was only US$8,512,373, while in the same period last year, it was US$12,941,913, a decrease of nearly 50 percent. Among the exported goods, textiles and their thick materials still accounted for the majority. In the first seven months of this year, the total value was US$30,776,142, accounting for about 40 percent of the total exports. Among them, raw silk alone was worth US$18,587,040, accounting for six-tenths of the raw materials for textiles and occupying the most important position in China's exports to the United States. In addition, tung oil, a non-edible plant product, was exported in the amount of 92,381,259 pounds in the seven months, worth US$8,724,098, also occupying the second most important position.

Shanghai County Government

Recent Major Policies Implemented 166

The Shanghai County Government has recently completed the resolution of the busy season tax collection fee, the re-appointment of charity association directors, and the investigation of the shipping situation. The details of the process are recorded below.

▲ Resolving the Tax Collection Fee Case: The county government previously received a report from the first district chief, stating that the township chiefs who undertake the busy season tax collection should be given a tax collection fee to ensure responsibility, etc. County Magistrate Yan instructed the Finance Bureau to convene another meeting to discuss the measures. It is reported that the bureau convened more than a dozen people, including the district chiefs of the six districts under the county and the director of the property department, on the afternoon of the 5th to discuss the measures. Bureau Chief Wang presided over the meeting. After the usual formalities, the case was discussed in detail, and the following was resolved: The tax collection fee should be completely transparent, with actual expenses paid for actual use. If there is a surplus, it should all be used as funding for the township office.

▲ Re-Appointing Charity Association Directors: The county government previously approved the consultation from the Songjiang County Government, stating that the term of office of the fourth session of the directors of the old Song Charity Association had expired. It requested the recommendation of the fifth session of directors for reply so that an appointment letter could be sent. County Magistrate Yan appointed Mr. Niu Changyao from the county to serve. The Songjiang County Government was consulted and replied on record. It is now approved that the county has consulted and replied, and an appointment letter for Mr. Niu has been attached. County Magistrate Yan has informed Mr. Niu to check and receive it.

▲ Investigating the Shipping Situation: Construction Bureau Chief Wu stated that the shipping industry is of great importance to transportation. There are quite a few small steamers operating within the county, but the bureau has no record of the organizational status of the various shipping companies, which makes management difficult. Therefore, he specially instructed the department to prepare a form and send it to each small steamer company to fill out in detail and report it promptly for statistics.

Special Committee of the Industrial and Commercial Management Association 168

▲Second Research Meeting of the Personnel Group

The Personnel Group of the Special Committee of the Chinese Industrial and Commercial Management Association held its second research meeting yesterday at the United General Association. Seven committee members attended, chaired by Director Xia Xiaofang. They discussed the factory personnel department organization plan drafted by committee members Liu Congqiang, Xu Zhiyi, and Cai Zhengya. After detailed discussion and slight revisions by the committee members, the revised version is recorded below: (A) The department shall have one director and be divided into five sections, each with one section chief. (1) The Personnel Section shall be responsible for the following matters: (a) Selecting employees, such as interviews, observations, assessments, resume reviews, and physical examinations. (b) Guiding new employees, such as regulations, department locations, first-aid locations, restrooms, badges, etc. (c) Assessing performance and recommending promotions and transfers. (d) Approving resignations and investigating absences. (e) Filling out employee forms. (f) Compiling employee statistics, such as verifying no promotion opportunities, family environment, poor health, and tardiness. (g) Investigating employee grievances. (2) The Public Welfare Section shall be responsible for the following matters: (a) Employee housing registration. (b) Employee rent investigation. (c) Leisure entertainment. (d) Sports. (e) Legal counsel. (f) Letter counsel. (g) Cooperatives, canteens, insurance, and savings. (3) The Research Section shall be responsible for the following matters: (a) Job analysis. (b) Statistical compilation. (c) Cost-of-living research. (d) Standard salary research. (e) Promotion guidance. (4) The Training Section shall be responsible for the following matters: (a) Compiling operational rules. (b) Company announcements. (c) Publishing publications. (d) Convening general meetings. (e) Popular lectures. (f) Cooperation with local education institutions. (g) Educational films. (h) Suggestion boxes. (5) The Hygiene Section shall be responsible for the following matters: (a) Examining employee bodies. (b) Diagnosing and treating diseases. (c) Providing first aid for injuries. (d) Giving vaccinations. (e) Visiting sick employees. (f) Factory hygiene. (g) Health lectures. (h) Diagnosing and treating the illnesses of employees' family members. (i) Researching ways to reduce occupational diseases.

Resolution of Labor-Management Issues in the Sauce Industry 170

The labor-management issues in the sauce garden industry have been resolved. At 2:00 PM the day before yesterday, representatives from both sides revised the terms at the association hall of the industry, located in Tongfu Lane, Qieduo Polo Road. A total of twenty-four items were agreed upon. The representatives of the management were Zhang Yuchi, Chen Weiwen, Wu Yin'zhi (Yu Bozheng acting), Song Xinggui (Tong Qianhe acting), Song Shaolan (Qin Tongshu acting), Chu Boshen, Shen Baoyuan, Pan Ruxing, and Zhu Yunsheng. The representatives of the labor were Shao Guoyong, Ren Jieting, Weng Ruifu, and Shen Pinwei. The district party representative was Hu Shouqi. The revised terms are recorded as follows: (1) The shop recognizes the right of the Shanghai Special City Sauce Industry Workers' Union to represent all its members (hereinafter referred to as "the workers"). (2) Workers shall not be dismissed without cause. If dismissed unjustly, it can be reported to the guild and the workers' union for investigation and resolution. (3) The management shall not employ private individuals or those outside the industry. If the shop has a vacancy, it must first hire members of the workers' union. (4) The minimum monthly salary for ordinary workers is 14 to 16 yuan; for "Pin Ge" (quality checker) and "Men Gang" (door keeper), 17 to 18 yuan; for "Pao Jie" (salesman) and "Fa Huo" (shipper), 19 to 20 yuan; for "Pi Zhang" (ledger clerk) and "Zhang Fang" (accountant), 21 to 23 yuan. The minimum monthly salary for ordinary office staff is 10 to 15 yuan. (5) Apprentices shall receive a monthly allowance of 14 yuan in the first year, 28 yuan in the second year, and 42 yuan in the third year. After three years of apprenticeship, their salary shall be equal to that of a staff member. However, those who are not up to the level of ordinary staff can be called trainees, with a monthly salary of 8 yuan. The training period is limited to one year. The number of apprentices shall be one for every ten staff members in the shop, two for more than ten, and three for more than twenty. Apprentices can only be added after three years, and the apprenticeship period is the same as for non-residential apprentices. (6) Wages are paid every five days of the month, and double wages are paid in December (double payment for the last five days of November and the salary for December). (7) Monthly regulations apply to all staff, workers and apprentices who shall receive a monthly sum of one silver dollar regardless of leave taken. Office staff are not included. (8) Each worker is allowed to be away from the shop 36 hours each month as standard, without any reduction in wages. This does not apply in cases of necessity. (9) If a worker's parents or wife die, or if the worker gets married, a special leave of three weeks shall be granted, with wages paid as usual, and the worker may also draw three months' salary in advance from the shop. (10) At the end of each year, the shop shall give each staff member 6 yuan for travel expenses and 3 yuan for staying up on New Year's Eve; office staff shall receive half. (11) The standard working day for workers is twelve hours. For each day extended by two hours, the shop shall compensate each person with a monthly subsidy of one silver dollar. (12) Managers, staff, and office staff shall receive equal treatment in terms of meals. If they have family members in Shanghai, they may take turns going home to stay overnight outside of working hours, without any reduction in wages. (13) If a worker is ill, it must be reported to the management, and the shop shall bear the medical expenses upon doctor's certification. The worker shall not be dismissed within five months during the treatment period, and wages must be paid as usual. This does not apply to venereal diseases and tuberculosis. If someone is injured or dies on the job, appropriate compensation shall be provided in addition to clothing and a coffin. (14) Four jiao (角) of silver dollars per dan (担) of returned gold are distributed, with ten shares allocated as follows: 1.8% to the manager, 0.9% to the accountant, 0.7% to the ledger clerk, 0.7% to the salesman, 0.6% to the shipper, 1.8% to the office staff, and the remaining 3.5% distributed proportionally to ordinary staff and students according to their salaries. (15) The shop shall provide apprentices with two hours of remedial arithmetic lessons every evening and bear the cost. Apprentices must not disobey legitimate instruction. However, the shop must not beat apprentices or order them to do work outside of their duties. Apprentices may also take turns participating in small group meetings convened by the union in the shop. (16) All holidays announced by the government shall be observed as days off, notified by the manager, and wages shall be paid as usual. (17) When the workers' union convenes a delegates' congress, each shop may send two or three representatives to participate, and wages shall be paid as usual for attending other meetings. (18) The workers and the shop owner shall share the shop's annual profits in a 30/70 split, with the distribution method being 2% to the manager, 1% to the accountant, 0.75% to the ledger clerk, 0.75% to the salesman, 0.5% to the shipper, 1.2% to the office staff, and the remaining 3.8% distributed proportionally to ordinary staff and students according to their salaries. (19) The shop must submit a report to the higher authorities if it reduces its scope of business, changes its business strategy, or ceases operations. (20) The business accounts must be made public. If there are any doubts, the union has the right to audit them together with the higher authorities. (21) Six jiao of silver dollars are extracted from each vat of sauce residue: four jiao to the office staff, and the remaining two jiao distributed proportionally to the manager, staff, and students according to their salaries. (22) All existing preferential practices shall not be cancelled. (23) The daily wage for bamboo craftsmen is four jiao of silver dollars, with each master limited to one apprentice. (24) The office staff shall handle upper and lower matters according to the old practices of each shop.

Reasons for Yesterday's Delay on the Beijing-Shanghai Train 171

▲Obstacles due to Rain Between Lücheng and Lingkou

Between Lücheng and Lingkou stations, at kilometer 179, continuous heavy rain had washed away three railroad ties and some gravel. The first express train from Ningbo to Shanghai, as well as the special express train and the slow trains of third and fourth class, were waiting for the road to be repaired, so they were all delayed by more than three hours.

National Goods Association L]

Telegram Urging Universal Promotion of National Goods 172

The China National Goods Maintenance Association, in order to establish National Goods Maintenance Associations throughout the country, specially sent a telegram to the Executive Committee of the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, saying: "We believe that concentrated forces have broad functions, a unified system achieves effective results, and practice is valued, while empty words are useless. Laws emphasize realization, and prestige naturally arises. The matter of promoting national goods in our country has been continuously advocated by the association for the past twenty years, with repeated efforts. Although the words 'national goods' have been deeply engraved in the minds of our compatriots, in reality, the effect is only equivalent to zero. This is because there are no responsible agencies in various provinces, cities, and counties, and publicity is not widespread. Moreover, we observe that the current mindset of our people is due to the weakness of patriotic ideas. Extravagant people have the mentality of admiring foreign goods and despising domestic products. Therefore, the urgent way to save the situation is to first rectify people's hearts and change their ideas, so as to reverse the declining trend and lay the foundation for a strong country. The association has repeatedly contributed its humble opinions, proposing that the government issue an order to all provinces, cities, counties, and villages to establish National Goods Maintenance Associations to be solely responsible for maintaining national goods, so as to revitalize the lost hearts of the people. Unexpectedly, national affairs have changed, the situation has changed, and the promotion of national goods has not only not seen any effect, but has also become like water getting deeper and fire getting hotter. All national goods, industrial, and commercial enterprises are showing signs of decline. In addition, national difficulties are becoming more urgent, and the people's wealth is becoming more exhausted. The times are pressing, the world is dangerous, and the situation is critical. The association, therefore, resolved at the 23rd meeting of the 19th Executive Committee to present a petition to the National Government, ordering all levels of party departments in provinces, cities, counties, villages, and townships across the country to guide the agricultural, industrial, commercial, and student groups under their jurisdiction to organize branches of the China National Goods Maintenance Association within seven days of receiving the document, to proceed uniformly, cooperate fully, and publicize widely, so as to rectify people's hearts and achieve great results. We respectfully send this telegram, earnestly requesting your esteemed office to consider the difficulties of the times, approve its implementation, so as to save the national crisis and alleviate the people's livelihood, and we pray for instructions to obey, for the convenience of the party."
